                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Reversible Phase Transition for Sodium Insertion in Anatase TiO2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei; Fukunishi, Mika; Morgan, Benjamin. J.; Borkiewicz, Olaf J.; Chapman, Karena W.; Pralong, Valerie; Maignan, Antoine; Lebedev, Oleg I.; Ma, Jiwei; Groult, Henri; Komaba, Shinichi; Dambournet, Damien</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1836-1844</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 is a potential neg. electrode for sodium-ion batteries.  The sodium storage mechanism is, however, still under debate, yet its comprehension is required to optimize the electrochem. properties.  To clarify the sodium storage mechanism occurring in anatase, both electrochem. and chem. routes are used from which similar trends are obtained.  During the first discharge, an irreversible plateau region is obsd. which corresponds to the insertion of Na+ within the interstitial sites of anatase and is accompanied by a drastic loss of the long-range order as revealed by X-ray diffraction, high resoln. of high angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscope (HAADF-STEM), and pair distribution function (PDF) anal.  Further structural anal. of the total scattering data indicates that the sodiated phase displays a layered-like rhombohedral R‾3m structure built from the stacking of Ti and Na slabs.  Because of the initial 3D network of anatase, the reduced phase shows strong disorder due to cationic intermixing between the Ti and Na slabs and the refined chem. formula is (Na0.43Ti0.57)3a.box.0.22(Na0.39Ti0.39)3bO2, where .box. refers to vacancy.  The presence of high valence Ti ions in the Na layers induces a contraction of the c-parameter as compared to the ordered phase.  Upon desodiation, the structure further amorphized and the local structure probed by PDF is shown to be similar to the anatase TiO2, suggesting that the 3D network is recovered.  The reversible sodium insertion/deinsertion is thus attributed to the rhombohedral active phase formed during the first discharge, and an oxidized phase featuring the local structure of anatase.  Due to the amorphous nature of the two phases, the potential-compn. curves are characterized by a sloping curve.  Finally, a comparison between the intercalation of lithium and sodium into anatase TiO2 performed by DFT calcns. confirmed that, for the sodiated phase, the rhombohedral structure is more stable than the tetragonal phase obsd. during the lithiation of nanoparticles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/cm503479h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Søndergaard, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mamakhel, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marinaro, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wohlfahrt-Mehrens, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wonsyld, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahl, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Iversen, B.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Re-oxidation reconstruction process of solid electrolyte interphase layer derived from highly active anion for potassium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Liang; Li, Jinliang; Wu, Tianhua; Sun, Peng; Tan, Shaozao; Wang, Hao; Xie, Weiguang; Pan, Likun; Yamauchi, Yusuke; Mai, Wenjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">87</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">106150</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In our work, we obtain molybdenum sulfide-reduced graphene oxide (MS-RGO) composite and find that variation of anion in electrolyte could significantly affect the stability of MS-RGO composite for potassium-ion batteries (KIBs).  Here, our MS-RGO composite presents a high capacity of 328 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 after 50 cycles and a stable capacity of 170 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles even at 1 A g-1.  We find that the anion of bisfluorosulfimide (FSI) in electrolyte can significantly improve the cycling stability compared with anion of hexafluorophosphate (PF).  The excellent performance of battery in FSI-contg. electrolyte should be attributed to the enhanced re-oxidn. reconstruction process of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer.  The imperceptible re-oxidn. reconstruction process of SEI layer under the effect of anion can be detected by differential capacitance anal. in each cycle.  Meanwhile, we also confirm that the reaction activity of anion is a crit. factor in detg. the reconstruction process of SEI layer and the improvement of electrochem. performance.  The enhanced re-oxidn. reconstruction process derived from highly active anion not only complements existing knowledge on the failure mechanism of SEI layer, but also presents a new principle for electrolyte design to improve the performance of metal sulfides anodes for KIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202102562"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Building Elastic Solid Electrolyte Interphases for Stabilizing Microsized Antimony Anodes in Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Building Elastic Solid Electrolyte Interphases for Stabilizing Microsized Antimony Anodes in Potassium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Du, Xiaoqiong; Gao, Yao; Zhang, Biao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2102562</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Alloy anodes composed of microsized particles receive increasing attention recently, which outperform the nanostructured counterparts in both the manufg. cost and volumetric energy d.  However, the pulverization of particles and fracture of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) during cycling brings about fast capacity degrdn.  Herein, it is shown how normally considered fragile SEI can become highly elastic through electrolyte chem. regulation.  Compared to the SEI constructed in classic carbonate electrolyte, the at. force microscopy tests reveal that the one built in ether-based electrolyte doubles the max. elastic strain to accommodate the repeated swelling-contracting.  Such an SEI effectively encapsulates the microsized Sb anodes to prevent the capacity loss from particle isolation.  Coupled with an intercalation-assisted alloying reaction mechanism, a sustained capacity of ≈573 mAh g-1 after 180 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 with outstanding initial Coulombic efficiency is obtained, which is among the highest values achieved in K-ion batteries.  This study emphasizes the significance of building robust SEI, which offers the opportunity to enable stable microsized alloy anodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref39" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.02.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Long Cycle Life and High Rate Sodium-Ion Chemistry for Hard Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">274</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">282</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unraveling mechanism of different kinetics performance between ether and carbonate ester electrolytes in hard carbon electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Xiaoli; Li, Xinhai; Zhong, Jing; Wang, Siwu; Wang, Zhixing; Guo, Huajun; Wang, Jiexi; Yan, Guochun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2209523</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ether electrolytes exhibit better rate kinetics than carbonate ester electrolytes when used in several kinds of anode materials, esp. in hard carbon (HC) for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the mechanism causing the remarkable kinetics difference is still unclear.  Here, a three-electrode system is used first to eliminate the influence of polarization from the Na counter electrode.  Then, there is systematic exploration from three steps of the electrode reaction process (Na+) storage in HC; de-solvation; Na+ migration through solid electrolyte interphase (SE), and the underlying mysteries are uncovered.  For Na+ storage in the bulk of the HC, it is found that two systems show the same storage mechanism and Na metallic nanoparticles will appear when discharged to 0.1 V.  In addn., faster de-solvation of the ether electrolyte is uncovered by three-electrode temp.-dependent EIS and solvation free energies calcn.  Moreover, the difference of the SEI layers is unraveled by XPS etching, SEM, and differential electrochem. mass spectrometry.  Most importantly, by discriminating the impacts of the SEI layers and de-solvation behavior, it can be concluded that the de-solvation process is the rate-controlling step of the electrode reaction process and is the main factor causing the kinetics differences between the two electrolytes.  The research provides a clear mechanism to illuminate fast kinetics for ether electrolytes, which will promote its application in SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.2c09997"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolyte Design Enabling Stable Solid Electrolyte Interface for High-Performance Silicon/Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte Design Enabling Stable Solid Electrolyte Interface for High-Performance Silicon/Carbon Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Ziyue; Wu, Feng; Li, Li; Chen, Nan; Luo, Guangqiu; Du, Jianguo; Zhao, Liyuan; Ma, Yue; Li, Yuejiao; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon (Si)-based materials have been considered as one of the most promising anodes for the development of high-energy-d. lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  However, poor interfacial stability and structural degrdn. are crit. challenges for the successful application of Si-based anodes in LIBs.  Herein, the use of a novel fluorinated carbonate (trifluoropropylene carbonate, TFPC) with high redn. potential and rapid film-forming ability as an electrolyte cosolvent is reported, which overcomes the deterioration of the electrode structure that hinders the battery quality.  XPS combined with Fourier transform IR spectroscopy technol. investigated the compn. and distribution of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer formed on the Si/C anode.  Notably, a stable SEI with an org. and inorg. bilayer structure was formed in this electrolyte design, and excellent mech. properties and ionic cond. were achieved.  Moreover, the Li intercalation mechanism is elucidated by in situ Raman characterization.  Benefited from this unique SEI, the Si/C-based batteries exhibit compelling cycling and rate performance.  This work provides an in-depth understanding of the Li intercalation mechanism of the Si/C electrode, as well as a novel electrolyte, for high-performance LIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202200397"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kuang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Harnessing Plasma-Assisted Doping Engineering to Stabilize Metallic Phase MoSe<sub>2</sub> for Fast and Durable Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv. Herein, a plasma-assisted P-doping-triggered phase-transition engineering is proposed to synthesize stabilized P-doped 1T phase MoSe2 nanoflower composites (P-1T-MoSe2 NFs). As a result, the P-1T-MoSe2 NFs deliver an exceptional high reversible capacity of 510.8 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 with no capacity fading over 1000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1 for sodium storage.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stabilizing metal battery anodes through the design of solid electrolyte interphases</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Qing; Stalin, Sanjuna; Archer, Lynden A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is a chem. distinct material phase formed by a combination of electrochem. redn. and chem. reactions at both the explicit and implicit interfaces in all electrochem. cells.  The structure, chem., and thermodn. of the materials that accumulate in such interfacial material phases have emerged over the last decade to play crucial roles in achieving high levels of anode reversibility in secondary batteries, esp. in systems where electrochem. active metals are used as anodes for high-energy-d. and cost-effective storage.  Here, we review the history, chem., formation characteristics, and approaches taken to achieve rational design of the SEI at metal anodes.  Strategies that explicitly take advantage of the redox chem. of electrolyte components to build designed, favorable SEI inside electrochem. cells, as well as those that benefit from ex situ chemistries performed outside the cell to create artificial SEI that enhance anode reversibility are highlighted.  Taking advances based on these methods as a point of departure, the review also considers interphase design rules that facilitate chem., mech., and electrochem. stability and fast ion transport through the SEI.  Finally, we discuss differences and similarities of SEI formed on monovalent (Li, Na, and K), divalent (Mg, Ca, and Zn), and trivalent (Al) metals of contemporary interest for developing cost-effective but high-performance anodes and on that basis, underscore the urgent need for intrusive exptl. tools for analyzing the SEI on metals at at. levels.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.1c01918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fast and Durable Potassium Storage Enabled by Constructing Stress-Dispersed Co3Se4 Nanocrystallites Anchored on Graphene Sheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Hehe; Cheng, Yong; Zhang, Qiaobao; Ye, Weibin; Yu, Xiaohua; Wang, Ming-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10107-10118</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal dichalcogenides are regarded as promising anode materials for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) because of their high theor. capacities.  However, due to the large at. radius of K+, the structural damage caused by the huge vol. expansion upon potassiation is much more severe than that of their lithium counterparts.  In this research, a stress-dispersed structure with Co3Se4 nanocrystallites orderly anchored on graphene sheets is achieved through a two-step hydrothermal treatment to alleviate the structural deterioration.  The ability to reduce the contact stress by the well-dispersed Co3Se4 nanocrystallites during K+ intercalation, together with the highly conductive graphene matrix, provides a more reliable and efficient anode architecture than its two agminated counterparts.  Given these advantages, the optimized electrode delivers excellent cycling stability (301.8 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 A g-1), as well as an outstanding rate capacity (203.8 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1).  Further in situ and ex situ characterizations and d. functional theory calcns. elucidate the potassium storage mechanism of Co3Se4 during the conversion reaction and reveal the fast electrochem. kinetics of the rationally designed electrode.  This work provides a practical approach for constructing stable metal-selenide anodes with long cycle life and high-rate performance for PIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b05865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anion Vacancies Regulating Endows MoSSe with Fast and Stable Potassium Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Huang, Dan; Gan, Qingmeng; Hao, Junnan; Liu, Sailin; Wu, Zhibin; Pang, Wei Kong; Johannessen, Bernt; Tang, Yougen; Luo, Jing-Li; Wang, Haiyan; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11843-11852</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Vacancy engineering is a promising approach for optimizing the energy storage performance of transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) due to the unique properties of vacancies in manipulating the electronic structure and active sites.  Nevertheless, achieving effective introduction of anion vacancies with adjustable vacancy concn. on a large scale is still a big challenge.  Herein, MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys with anion vacancies introduced in situ have been achieved by a simple alloying reaction, and the vacancy concn. has been optimized through adjusting the chem. compn.  Exptl. and d. functional theory calcn. results suggest that the anion vacancies in MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys could enhance the electronic cond., induce more active sites, and alleviate structural variation in the alloys during the potassium storage process.  When applied as potassium ion battery anodes, the most optimized vacancy-rich MoSSe alloy delivered high reversible capacities of 517.4 and 362.4 mAh g-1 at 100 and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  Moreover, a reversible capacity of 220.5 mAh g-1 could be maintained at 2000 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles.  This work demonstrates a practical approach to modifying the electronic and defect properties of TMDs, providing an effective strategy for constructing advanced electrode materials for battery systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref50" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1038/nchem.2470"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Busche, M.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dynamic formation of a solid-liquid electrolyte interphase and its consequences for hybrid-battery concepts</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Busche, Martin R.; Drossel, Thomas; Leichtweiss, Thomas; Weber, Dominik A.; Falk, Mareike; Schneider, Meike; Reich, Maria-Louisa; Sommer, Heino; Adelhelm, Philipp; Janek, Juergen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Chemistry</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The discharging and charging of batteries require ion transfer across phase boundaries.  In conventional lithium-ion batteries, Li+ ions have to cross the liq. electrolyte and only need to pass the electrode interfaces.  Future high-energy batteries may need to work as hybrids, and so serially combine a liq. electrolyte and a solid electrolyte to suppress unwanted redox shuttles.  This adds new interfaces that might significantly decrease the cycling-rate capability.  Here it is shown that the interface between a typical fast-ion-conducting solid electrolyte and a conventional liq. electrolyte is chem. unstable and forms a resistive solid-liq. electrolyte interphase (SLEI).  Insights into the kinetics of this new type of interphase are obtained by impedance studies of a two-chamber cell.  The chem. of the SLEI, its growth with time and the effect of water impurities are examd. by state-of-the-art surface anal. and depth profiling.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref51" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/S0167-2738(03)00150-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barsoukov, E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Comparison of Kinetic Properties of LiCoO<sub>2</sub> and LiTi<sub>0.05</sub>Mg<sub>0.05</sub>Ni<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> by Impedance Spectroscopy</span>. <i>Solid State Ionics</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2003</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>161</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">19</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">29</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">New material based on LiNiO2 with some nickel atoms substituted for other metals has become increasingly popular as cathode materials for Li-ion battery due to higher capacity of LiNiO2 compared to traditionally used LiCoO2 and improved material stability and safety due to substitutes.  However, rate capability of new materials was not extensively researched.  The purpose of this investigation is to characterize by impedance spectroscopy all major kinetic steps of Li intercalation into conventional LiCoO2 and substitution-stabilized material LiTi0.05Mg0.05Ni0.7Co0.2O2 samples, provided by FMC.  Wide frequency range of impedance measurements (to 200 μHz) with acceptable duration was made possible by using Kumho Chem. Labs.' one-shot FFT-impedance spectrometer.  Availability of such low frequency data allowed confident estn. of diffusion and phase-change kinetic parameters.  Results were analyzed in terms of transmission line model considering composite structure of electrode.  Effects of particle size and mechanism of sample degrdn. with cycling were also investigated.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref52" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104895"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sa, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mathur, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Breaking the Limitation of Sodium-Ion Storage for Nanostructured Carbon Anode by Engineering Desolvation Barrier with Neat Electrolytes</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>74</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">104895</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Breaking the limitation of sodium-ion storage for nanostructured carbon anode by engineering desolvation barrier with neat electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhen, Yichao; Sa, Rongjian; Zhou, Kaiqiang; Ding, Lingyi; Chen, Yang; Mathur, Sanjay; Hong, Zhensheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">74</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104895</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the past, most of the studies monotonously focused on developing electrode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), while the compatibility effects and mechanism of electrolytes with material microstructures on the sodiation behavior are barely involved.  Here, we demonstrate the sodium-ion storage behavior of carbon anode in neat ether electrolytes with outstanding ion diffusion kinetics at electrode surface that breaks its innate limitation.  Porous nanocarbon with small interlayer spacing but very high surface area exhibits a record high ICE over 91.1% and exceptional rate capability for Na-ion storage in ether-based electrolytes.  This is due to the remarkably reduced Na+ desolvation barrier in ether electrolytes (~ 94.6 meV) that is less than one-third of that in ester electrolytes (~ 307.8 meV).  The strong interaction of Na-ions with ester electrolytes and their decompn. on electrode surface can be suppressed by adopting ether solvents owing to lower Gibbs free energies of solvation and Na+ desolvation energy as revealed by DFT calcns.  For electrode materials working with ether electrolytes, a large surface area is crit. for better electrochem. performance.  This study provides a reliable regulation parameter for tailoring electrolytes with materials that offers promising potential for nanostructured materials toward high-rate rechargeable devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="9318833b592a54b8-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47'],'ref48':['cit48'],'ref49':['cit49'],'ref50':['cit50'],'ref51':['cit51'],'ref52':['cit52']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

        </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.1021/jacsau.1c00158"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Revisit Electrolyte Chemistry of Hard Carbon in Ether for Na Storage</span>. <i>JACS Au</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1208</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1216</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacsau.1c00158</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Revisit Electrolyte Chemistry of Hard Carbon in Ether for Na Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Jun; Sun, Yi-yang; Yan, Yehao; Feng, Lei; Zhang, Yifan; Lin, Aming; Huang, Fuqiang; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">JACS Au</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1208-1216</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JAAUCR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2691-3704</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons (HC) as an anode material in sodium ion batteries, present enhanced electrochem. performances in ether-based electrolytes, making them promising potential in practical applications.  However, the underlying mechanism behind the excellent performances is still in question.  Here, ex-situ NMR, gas chromatog.-mass spectrometry and high-resoln. transmission electron microscope were used to clarify the insightful chem. of ether- and ester-based electrolytes in terms of solid-electrolyte-interphase (SEI) on hard carbons.  The results confirm the marked electrolyte decompn. and the formation of a SEI film in EC/DEC, but no SEI film in the case of diglyme.  In-situ electrochem. quartz crystal microbalance and mol. dynamics support that ether mols. have been cointercalated into hard carbons likely.  To our knowledge, these results are reported for the first time.  It might be very useful for the rational design of advanced electrode materials based on HC in future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202200475"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, P. F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, S. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y. G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H. Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrode-Electrolyte Interfacial Chemistry Modulation for Ultra-High Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>61</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e202200475</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.202200475</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode-Electrolyte Interfacial Chemistry Modulation for Ultra-High Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Zheng; Wang, Hong; Wu, Peng-Fei; Zhou, Si-Yu; Huang, Yuan-Cheng; Zhang, Rui; Sun, Dan; Tang, You-Gen; Wang, Hai-Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">61</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">e202200475</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries capable of operating at rate and temp. extremes are highly desirable, but elusive due to the dynamics and thermodn. limitations.  Herein, a strategy of electrode-electrolyte interfacial chem. modulation is proposed.  The com. hard carbon demonstrates superior rate performance with 212 mAh g-1 at an ultra-high c.d. of 5 A g-1 in the electrolyte with weak ion solvation/desolvation, which is much higher than those in common electrolytes (nearly no capacity in carbonate-based electrolytes).  Even at -20°C, a high capacity of 175 mAh g-1 (74% of its room-temp. capacity) can be maintained at 2 A g-1.  Such an electrode retains 90% of its initial capacity after 1000 cycles.  As proven, weak ion solvation/desolvation of THF greatly facilitates fast-ion diffusion at the SEI/electrolyte interface and homogeneous SEI with well-distributed NaF and org. components ensures fast Na+ diffusion through the SEI layer and a stable interface.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-019-08506-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.-B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Evolution of the Electrochemical Interface in Sodium Ion Batteries with Ether Electrolytes</span>. <i>Nat. Here we show that coupling titanium dioxide and other anode materials with diglyme does enable higher efficiency and reversible capacity than those for the combination involving ester electrolytes.  Importantly, the electrolyte dependent performance is revealed to be the result of the different structural evolution induced by a varied sodiation depth.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be strong candidates for large-scale energy storage with the benefits of cost-effectiveness and sodium abundance.  Reliable electrolytes, as ionic conductors that regulate the electrochem. reaction behavior and the nature of the interface and electrode, are indispensable in the development of advanced SIBs with high Coulombic efficiency, stable cycling performance and high rate capability.  Conventional carbonate-based electrolytes encounter numerous obstacles for their wide application in SIBs due to the formation of a dissolvable, continuous-thickening solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer and inferior stability with electrodes.  Comparatively, ether-based electrolytes (EBEs) are emerging in the secondary battery field with fascinating properties to improve the performance of batteries, esp. SIBs.  Their stable solvation structure enables highly reversible solvent-co-intercalation reactions and the formation of a thin and stable SEI.  However, although EBEs can provide more stable cycling and rapid sodiation kinetics in electrodes, benefitting from their favorable electrolyte/electrode interactions such as chem. compatibility and good wettability, their special chem. is still being investigated and puzzling.  In this review, we provide a thorough and comprehensive overview on the developmental history, fundamental characteristics, superiorities and mechanisms of EBEs, together with their advances in other battery systems.  Notably, the relation among electrolyte science, interfacial chem. and electrochem. performance is highlighted, which is of great significance for the in-depth understanding of battery chem.  Finally, future perspectives and potential directions are proposed to navigate the design and optimization of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces for advanced batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2022.107693"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Que, L.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.-B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Utilizing Weakly-Solvated Diglyme-Based Electrolyte to Achieve a 10,000-Cycles Durable Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Cathode Endured at −20 °C</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>102</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">107693</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

This unique structure consists of a tunable nanorod core, interstitial hollow spaces, and a functional nanotube shell assembled from two-dimensional nanosheets.  By adjusting the types of solvents used and reaction time, the morphologies of TiO2/C composites can be tuned to nanoparticles, microrods, rod-in-tube structures, or microtubes. In operando high-energy X-ray diffraction further confirms the stable crystal structure of the rod-in-tube TiO2/C during Na+ insertion/extn.  This work highlights that nanostructure design is an effective strategy to achieve advanced energy storage materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.09.044"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">TiO<sub>2</sub>@C Nanosheets with Highly Exposed (001) Facets as a High-Capacity Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">With the properties of high theor. capacity and excellent structural stability, TiO2 has been widely studied as anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  In this work, a composite structure of ultra-small TiO2 nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanosheets (TCNS) is obtained by annealing polyvinylpyrrolidone coated Zn-Ti layered double hydroxide under inert atm., with zinc species removed by hydrochloric acid.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been widely investigated as one of the most promising candidates for replacing lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  For SIBs or LIBs, designing a stable and uniform solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) at the electrode-electrolyte interface is the key factor to provide high capacity, long-term cycling, and high-rate performance.  In this paper, it is described how a remarkably enhanced SEI layer can be obtained on TiO2 nanotube (TiO2 NTs) arrays that allows for a strongly improved performance of sodium battery systems.  Key is that a Li+ pre-insertion in TiO2 NTs can condition the SEI for Na+ replacement.  SIBs constructed with Li-pre-inserted NTs deliver an exceptional Na+ cycling stability (e.g., 99.9 ± 0.1% capacity retention during 250 cycles at a current rate of 50 mA g-1) and an excellent rate capability (e.g., 132 mA h g-1 at a current rate of 1 A g-1).  The key factor in this outstanding performance is that Li-pre-insertion into TiO2 NTs leads not only to an enhanced electronic cond. in the tubes, but also expands the anatase lattice for facilitated subsequent Na+ cycling.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202214717"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dual-Function Presodiation with Sodium Diphenyl Ketone towards Ultra-stable Hard Carbon Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew. In addn., combined effect of additives facilitates the formation of additive-derived LiF-Li3N enhanced inorg.-rich SEI, significantly reducing the Li+ diffusion energy barrier and promoting compact chunky Li deposition.         </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance magnesium electrolyte is crucial for the practical application of rechargeable Mg batteries. Theor. calcns. and exptl. characterizations reveal that the pos. electrostatic potential distributed around the hydrogen atoms in a BTFE mol. could interact with Cl- and facilitate the formation of charged, instead of neutral, ion-solvent clusters in the BTFE cosolvated magnesium lithium chloride complex (MLCC) electrolyte, which helps to lift its ionic cond.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Li+ solvation structure (LSS) is considered to be the decisive factor in detg. the electrochem. performance of lithium metal batteries.  Herein, we propose a phase change electrolyte (PCE) whose LSS can be in operando regulated by changing the phys. state of the electrolyte.  The primary solvent of a PCE is di-Me dodecanedioate (DDCA), which stands out among a series of solvents, exhibiting excellent comprehensive performance.                         rightTab-cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Optimisation of sodium-based energy storage cells using pre-sodiation: a perspective on the emerging field</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dewar, Daniel; Glushenkov, Alexey M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable sodium-based energy storage cells (sodium-ion batteries, sodium-based dual-ion batteries and sodium-ion capacitors) are currently enjoying enormous attention from the research community due to their promise to replace or complement lithium-ion cells in multiple applications.  In all of these emerging sodium-based systems, their performances are worsened by a range of undesired complications, including insufficient initial content of sodium ions in a cell, poor initial coulombic efficiencies of electrode materials, loss of sodium ions during long-term cycling, and the lack of practical possibility to optimize potential ranges in neg. and pos. electrodes.  Pre-sodiation has emerged as an appealing technique to alleviate these problems and, therefore, to increase the practical energy densities of these devices.  Nevertheless, the concept of pre-sodiation appears to be under-appreciated within the community, despite the fact that parallel methods of pre-lithiation find more and more uses in the established lithium-based energy storage cells.  The intent of this timely perspective is to educate the community on the important benefits of pre-sodiation for a broad range of sodium-based energy storage cells and provide an up-to-date overview of this emerging field.  A detailed summary of various situations where pre-sodiation is needed is provided, followed by the crit. anal. of electrochem. and chem. techniques used for this purpose.  An emphasis is made on the commercialisation potential of the optimal pre-sodiation procedures, and suggestions are provided for the areas of future advancement in the field.  This perspective provides important insights of a broad interest to a multidisciplinary community of energy scientists, materials chemists and engineers working at the interface of new energy storage chemistries, device engineering and relevant materials science.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202005581"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prelithiation/Presodiation Techniques for Advanced Electrochemical Energy Storage Systems: Concepts, Applications, and Perspectives</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Prelithiation/presodiation techniques are regarded as indispensable procedures in electrochem. energy storage (EES) systems, which can effectively compensate irreversible capacity loss, raise working voltage, and increase Li+/Na+ concn. in the electrolyte.  Various prelithiation/presodiation methods have been successfully exploited and a revolutionary impact has been achieved through the utilization of prelithiation/presodiation techniques.  It is well acknowledged that different prelithiation/presodiation strategies possess their own specific mechanisms, which play vital roles in the advancement of EES systems.  However, there has rarely been systematical reviews about the concept and progress of prelithiation/presodiation techniques.  Hence, in this review various prelithiation/presodiation approaches are comprehensively analyzed and summarized, and in-depth prelithiation/presodiation behaviors and other innovative applications (including optimization of separators, amelioration of binders, regeneration of spent batteries) are discussed in detail.  Finally, suggested future directions of prelithiation/presodiation techniques are proposed and it is expected that these prelithiation/presodiation techniques could provide guidance for construction of advanced EES systems and propel the commercialization process with a focus on safety considerations.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b14381"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moeez, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, H.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, H.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">There is a growing demand for high-rate rechargeable batteries for powering elec. vehicles and portable electronics.  Here, we demonstrate a strategy for improving electrode performance by controlling the formation of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI).  A composite electrode consisting of hard carbon (HC) and carbon nanotubes (CNTs) was used to study the formation of the SEI at different charging rates in an electrolyte consisting of 1 M NaClO4 in a mixed solvent with ethylene carbonate (EC) and propylene carbonate (PC), as well as fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) additive.  The half-cell method was used to form the SEI at different charging rates (e.g., 1, 10, and 100 A/g).  Sym. capacitor cells were employed to study ion transport properties through the SEI.  It was found that the SEI is a primary factor responsible for limiting the capacity of the composite anode material in conventional ester-based electrolytes.  The electrode with the SEI formed at 100 A/g exhibited the lowest impedance and delivered nearly twice the capacity of the electrode with the SEI formed at 1 A/g.  This significant difference is due to a thin SEI formed at the fast charging rate, as has been obsd. with ether-based electrolytes.  An identical decay rate (0.11 mA h/g per cycle) was obsd. on the electrodes with SEIs formed at different charging rates in an ester electrolyte.  No chem. difference among the three SEI layers was found.  However, morphol. differences of the SEI layers were obsd.  This difference is believed to account for the different electrochem. behaviors of the electrodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein we investigate the influence of the sodium salt anion on the performance of Na-O2 batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 is a potential neg. electrode for sodium-ion batteries.  The sodium storage mechanism is, however, still under debate, yet its comprehension is required to optimize the electrochem. properties.  To clarify the sodium storage mechanism occurring in anatase, both electrochem. and chem. routes are used from which similar trends are obtained.  During the first discharge, an irreversible plateau region is obsd. which corresponds to the insertion of Na+ within the interstitial sites of anatase and is accompanied by a drastic loss of the long-range order as revealed by X-ray diffraction, high resoln. of high angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscope (HAADF-STEM), and pair distribution function (PDF) anal.  Further structural anal. of the total scattering data indicates that the sodiated phase displays a layered-like rhombohedral R‾3m structure built from the stacking of Ti and Na slabs.  Because of the initial 3D network of anatase, the reduced phase shows strong disorder due to cationic intermixing between the Ti and Na slabs and the refined chem. formula is (Na0.43Ti0.57)3a.box.0.22(Na0.39Ti0.39)3bO2, where .box. refers to vacancy.  The presence of high valence Ti ions in the Na layers induces a contraction of the c-parameter as compared to the ordered phase.  Upon desodiation, the structure further amorphized and the local structure probed by PDF is shown to be similar to the anatase TiO2, suggesting that the 3D network is recovered.  The reversible sodium insertion/deinsertion is thus attributed to the rhombohedral active phase formed during the first discharge, and an oxidized phase featuring the local structure of anatase.  Due to the amorphous nature of the two phases, the potential-compn. curves are characterized by a sloping curve.  Finally, a comparison between the intercalation of lithium and sodium into anatase TiO2 performed by DFT calcns. confirmed that, for the sodiated phase, the rhombohedral structure is more stable than the tetragonal phase obsd. during the lithiation of nanoparticles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1021/cm503479h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Søndergaard, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mamakhel, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marinaro, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wohlfahrt-Mehrens, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wonsyld, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahl, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Iversen, B. However, the mechanism causing the remarkable kinetics difference is still unclear.  Here, a three-electrode system is used first to eliminate the influence of polarization from the Na counter electrode.  Then, there is systematic exploration from three steps of the electrode reaction process (Na+) storage in HC; de-solvation; Na+ migration through solid electrolyte interphase (SE), and the underlying mysteries are uncovered. Most importantly, by discriminating the impacts of the SEI layers and de-solvation behavior, it can be concluded that the de-solvation process is the rate-controlling step of the electrode reaction process and is the main factor causing the kinetics differences between the two electrolytes.  The research provides a clear mechanism to illuminate fast kinetics for ether electrolytes, which will promote its application in SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.2c09997"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolyte Design Enabling Stable Solid Electrolyte Interface for High-Performance Silicon/Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic-phase selenide molybdenum (1T-MoSe2) has become a rising star for sodium storage in comparison with its semiconductor phase (2H-MoSe2) owing to the intrinsic metallic electronic cond. and unimpeded Na+ diffusion structure.  However, the thermodynamically unstable nature of 1T phase renders it an unprecedented challenge to realize its phase control and stabilization.  Herein, a plasma-assisted P-doping-triggered phase-transition engineering is proposed to synthesize stabilized P-doped 1T phase MoSe2 nanoflower composites (P-1T-MoSe2 NFs).  Mechanism anal. reveals significantly decreased phase-transition energy barriers of the plasma-induced Se-vacancy-rich MoSe2 from 2H to 1T owing to its low crystallinity and reduced structure stability.  The vacancy-rich structure promotes highly concd. P doping, which manipulates the electronic structure of the MoSe2 and urges its phase transition, acquiring a high transition efficiency of 91% accompanied with ultrahigh phase stability.  As a result, the P-1T-MoSe2 NFs deliver an exceptional high reversible capacity of 510.8 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 with no capacity fading over 1000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1 for sodium storage.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanostructure designing has been showing great potential in improving the sodium storage performance of nanomaterials.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Fast charging and high volumetric capacity are two of the crit. demands for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is a chem. distinct material phase formed by a combination of electrochem. redn. and chem. reactions at both the explicit and implicit interfaces in all electrochem. cells.  The structure, chem., and thermodn. of the materials that accumulate in such interfacial material phases have emerged over the last decade to play crucial roles in achieving high levels of anode reversibility in secondary batteries, esp. in systems where electrochem. active metals are used as anodes for high-energy-d. and cost-effective storage.  Here, we review the history, chem., formation characteristics, and approaches taken to achieve rational design of the SEI at metal anodes.  Strategies that explicitly take advantage of the redox chem. of electrolyte components to build designed, favorable SEI inside electrochem. cells, as well as those that benefit from ex situ chemistries performed outside the cell to create artificial SEI that enhance anode reversibility are highlighted.  Taking advances based on these methods as a point of departure, the review also considers interphase design rules that facilitate chem., mech., and electrochem. stability and fast ion transport through the SEI.  Finally, we discuss differences and similarities of SEI formed on monovalent (Li, Na, and K), divalent (Mg, Ca, and Zn), and trivalent (Al) metals of contemporary interest for developing cost-effective but high-performance anodes and on that basis, underscore the urgent need for intrusive exptl. tools for analyzing the SEI on metals at at. levels.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.1c01918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal dichalcogenides are regarded as promising anode materials for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) because of their high theor. capacities. In this research, a stress-dispersed structure with Co3Se4 nanocrystallites orderly anchored on graphene sheets is achieved through a two-step hydrothermal treatment to alleviate the structural deterioration.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
