            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Vacancy engineering is a promising approach for optimizing the energy storage performance of transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) due to the unique properties of vacancies in manipulating the electronic structure and active sites.  Nevertheless, achieving effective introduction of anion vacancies with adjustable vacancy concn. on a large scale is still a big challenge.  Herein, MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys with anion vacancies introduced in situ have been achieved by a simple alloying reaction, and the vacancy concn. has been optimized through adjusting the chem. compn.  Exptl. and d. functional theory calcn. results suggest that the anion vacancies in MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys could enhance the electronic cond., induce more active sites, and alleviate structural variation in the alloys during the potassium storage process.  When applied as potassium ion battery anodes, the most optimized vacancy-rich MoSSe alloy delivered high reversible capacities of 517.4 and 362.4 mAh g-1 at 100 and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  Moreover, a reversible capacity of 220.5 mAh g-1 could be maintained at 2000 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles.  This work demonstrates a practical approach to modifying the electronic and defect properties of TMDs, providing an effective strategy for constructing advanced electrode materials for battery systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1038/nchem.2470"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Busche, M. R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Drossel, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Leichtweiss, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weber, D. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Falk, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schneider, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reich, M.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sommer, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Adelhelm, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Janek, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dynamic Formation of a Solid-Liquid Electrolyte Interphase and Its Consequences for Hybrid-Battery Concepts</span>. <i>Nat. Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">426</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">434</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nchem.2470</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dynamic formation of a solid-liquid electrolyte interphase and its consequences for hybrid-battery concepts</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Busche, Martin R.; Drossel, Thomas; Leichtweiss, Thomas; Weber, Dominik A.; Falk, Mareike; Schneider, Meike; Reich, Maria-Louisa; Sommer, Heino; Adelhelm, Philipp; Janek, Juergen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">426-434</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAHBB</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1755-4330</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The discharging and charging of batteries require ion transfer across phase boundaries.  In conventional lithium-ion batteries, Li+ ions have to cross the liq. electrolyte and only need to pass the electrode interfaces.  Future high-energy batteries may need to work as hybrids, and so serially combine a liq. electrolyte and a solid electrolyte to suppress unwanted redox shuttles.  This adds new interfaces that might significantly decrease the cycling-rate capability.  Here it is shown that the interface between a typical fast-ion-conducting solid electrolyte and a conventional liq. electrolyte is chem. unstable and forms a resistive solid-liq. electrolyte interphase (SLEI).  Insights into the kinetics of this new type of interphase are obtained by impedance studies of a two-chamber cell.  The chem. of the SLEI, its growth with time and the effect of water impurities are examd. by state-of-the-art surface anal. and depth profiling.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1016/S0167-2738(03)00150-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barsoukov, E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Comparison of Kinetic Properties of LiCoO<sub>2</sub> and LiTi<sub>0.05</sub>Mg<sub>0.05</sub>Ni<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> by Impedance Spectroscopy</span>. <i>Solid State Ionics</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2003</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>161</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">19</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">29</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/S0167-2738(03)00150-4</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Comparison of kinetic properties of LiCoO2 and LiTi0.05Mg0.05Ni0.7Co0.2O2 by impedance spectroscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Barsoukov, E.; Kim, D. H.; Lee, H.-S.; Lee, H.; Yakovleva, Marina; Gao, Yuan; Engel, John F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solid State Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2003</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">161</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1,2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">19-29</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSIOD3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-2738</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">New material based on LiNiO2 with some nickel atoms substituted for other metals has become increasingly popular as cathode materials for Li-ion battery due to higher capacity of LiNiO2 compared to traditionally used LiCoO2 and improved material stability and safety due to substitutes.  However, rate capability of new materials was not extensively researched.  The purpose of this investigation is to characterize by impedance spectroscopy all major kinetic steps of Li intercalation into conventional LiCoO2 and substitution-stabilized material LiTi0.05Mg0.05Ni0.7Co0.2O2 samples, provided by FMC.  Wide frequency range of impedance measurements (to 200 μHz) with acceptable duration was made possible by using Kumho Chem. Labs.' one-shot FFT-impedance spectrometer.  Availability of such low frequency data allowed confident estn. of diffusion and phase-change kinetic parameters.  Results were analyzed in terms of transmission line model considering composite structure of electrode.  Effects of particle size and mechanism of sample degrdn. with cycling were also investigated.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref52" class="rightTabRefNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit52" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104895"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sa, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mathur, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Breaking the Limitation of Sodium-Ion Storage for Nanostructured Carbon Anode by Engineering Desolvation Barrier with Neat Electrolytes</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>74</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">104895</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104895</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Breaking the limitation of sodium-ion storage for nanostructured carbon anode by engineering desolvation barrier with neat electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhen, Yichao; Sa, Rongjian; Zhou, Kaiqiang; Ding, Lingyi; Chen, Yang; Mathur, Sanjay; Hong, Zhensheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">74</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104895</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the past, most of the studies monotonously focused on developing electrode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), while the compatibility effects and mechanism of electrolytes with material microstructures on the sodiation behavior are barely involved.  Here, we demonstrate the sodium-ion storage behavior of carbon anode in neat ether electrolytes with outstanding ion diffusion kinetics at electrode surface that breaks its innate limitation.  Porous nanocarbon with small interlayer spacing but very high surface area exhibits a record high ICE over 91.1% and exceptional rate capability for Na-ion storage in ether-based electrolytes.  This is due to the remarkably reduced Na+ desolvation barrier in ether electrolytes (~ 94.6 meV) that is less than one-third of that in ester electrolytes (~ 307.8 meV).  The strong interaction of Na-ions with ester electrolytes and their decompn. on electrode surface can be suppressed by adopting ether solvents owing to lower Gibbs free energies of solvation and Na+ desolvation energy as revealed by DFT calcns.  For electrode materials working with ether electrolytes, a large surface area is crit. for better electrochem. performance.  This study provides a reliable regulation parameter for tailoring electrolytes with materials that offers promising potential for nanostructured materials toward high-rate rechargeable devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i11">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c07402?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c07402</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Schematic illustration of the reaction mechanism; XRD patterns and Raman spectra; the initial charge/discharge profiles; cycling performance; optical images; EDS mapping; cross-sectional SEM images; XPS etching spectra; CV curves; discharge/charge profiles at various current densities; EIS spectra after cycling; GITT potential profile; temperature-dependent Nyquist plots; and high-resolution (HRTEM) images (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c07402/suppl_file/am3c07402_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c07402/suppl_file/am3c07402_si_001.pdf">am3c07402_si_001.pdf (1.8 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {

	    }

	});

<script nonce="9318833b592a54b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="9318833b592a54b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

    /* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.

	*/

    var infoCentralCapture = (function () {
      //Detect mobile device
      window.mobilecheck = function () {
        var check = false;
        (function (a) {
          if (
            /(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera m(ob|in)i|palm( os)?|phone|p(ixi|re)\/|plucker|pocket|psp|series(4|6)0|symbian|treo|up\.(browser|link)|vodafone|wap|windows ce|xda|xiino/i.test(

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
